## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration (dA/dt) as a function of concentration (A) and time (t), which is fundamental to reaction kinetics. It describes how reactants are consumed or products form over time, typically governed by power laws, adsorption isotherms, autocatalytic feedback, or time-dependent catalyst deactivation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (simple unimolecular reaction)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular collision between identical species)
- Fractional-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (complex mechanisms or diffusion-controlled reactions)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (heterogeneous catalysis with competitive surface adsorption)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (reaction rate enhanced by product accumulation)
- Elovich-type kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * A) (surface desorption with exponential site energy distribution)
- Catalyst deactivation model: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (reaction rate modulated by time-dependent catalyst decay)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 / (1 + c1 * A) (transition behavior between first and second order mechanisms)
- Induction period kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 - exp(c1 * t)) (delayed reaction onset due to intermediate accumulation)
- Gompertz-type decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A * log(c1 * A) (log-log rate dependence in complex polymerization networks)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Monotonic reactant depletion â†’ Negative rate expression proportional to A or A**n
- Autocatalytic feedback â†’ Product term A * (c0 - A) or A * log(c0 * A) causing initial rate acceleration
- Catalyst deactivation/aging â†’ Multiplicative time factor exp(c * t) or (1 + c * t)**c modulating the base rate
- Competing parallel pathways â†’ Polynomial combination c0 * A - c1 * A**2 representing simultaneous formation and consumption
- Induction/delay period â†’ Time-activation factor (1 - exp(c * t)) scaling the instantaneous rate before full reaction onset
- Diffusion-controlled transport â†’ Square-root dependence sqrt(A) or fractional power A**c (0 < c < 1) indicating mass transfer limitations
- Reversible equilibrium balance â†’ Difference of power terms c0 * A**c1 - c1 * A**c2 representing forward and reverse reaction rates
- Heterogeneous site distribution â†’ Elovich-type exponential exp(c * A) or logarithmic log(c * A) dependence reflecting non-uniform active sites
